time = the period of minutes, days, weeks, years when things happen (time, times, timed, timing)

title = the name of something like a story, book, song, show, or movie; sometimes a word like ‘Dr.’ or ‘Mrs.’ or ‘General’ used before a person’s name (title, titles, titled, titling)

tobacco = a plant with big, sticky leaves used for chewing or for smoking in pipes, cigars, or cigarettes 

toil = long, hard work; or to use a lot of energy to do something (toil, toils, toiled, toiling)

toil-worn = showing a lot of wear-and-tear; looking very old because it has been used a lot 

tomb = a structure made to hold one or more dead bodies (tomb, tombs; tomblike)

tone = a single simple sound, such as a beep; sometimes means a sound that expresses a person’s feeling; sometimes means the shade of a color (tone, tones)

torment = how it feels to be hurt very badly; to make someone hurt or feel very bad (torment; torments; tormented; tormenting; tormentor, tormentors)

torture	 = made to feel extreme, terrible pain (torture, tortures, tortured, torturing; torturer)

total = the full amount of something; or to count items or numbers to get the full amount (total, totals, totaled, totaling)

trace = a sign that something happened or was there before; or a very small amount of something; sometimes means to follow, to look for, or find; sometimes means to copy by following the lines (trace, traces, traced, tracing; tracer, tracers) 

trade = to give one thing to get another thing; to buy and sell; sometimes means a job requiring a special skill like carpentry or pottery (trade, trades, traded, trading; trader, traders)

train = a large engine that pulls cars on two metal rails; sometimes a long moving line of things; sometimes teaching a person or animal to do something; sometimes a long part of a dress that trails behind (train, trains, trained, training; trainer; trainers

trait = a quality or feature of a person, animal, or thing, like a good sense of humor or getting angry very quickly (trait, traits)

tranquil = calm, quiet, peaceful (tranquil, tranquility)

transaction = trading for something, paying for something, doing business (transact, transacts, transacted, transacting; transaction, transactions)

transfer = to move something from one place to another place; to change from one bus, plane, or train to another (transfer, transfers, transferred, transferring) 

transform = to change something completely, especially the shape of something (transform, transforms, transformed, transforming; transformer, transformers)

tray = a large, flat plat, often used to carry food (tray, trays)

treachery = to purposely break a very important promise; to betray someone (treachery; treacheries; treacherous)

treat = how a person acts towards someone, being helpful or cruel or ignoring them; can mean doing something or giving something that makes a person happy (treat, treats, treated, treating; treatment)

trespass = to go somewhere or do something without permission; sometimes means to sin or do something bad (trespass, trespasses, trespassed, trespassing; trespasser, trespassers)

trial = when judge and jury decide if someone is guilty or innocent; can mean something very difficult to do; can mean to test or try out something (trial, trials)

trick = to fool, or prank, or lie to, or cheat someone (trick, tricks, tricked, tricking; trickery; trickster, tricksters)

trifle = small, unimportant, not a big deal, something with little value; to act like something is not important or has very little value (trifle, trifles, trifled, trifling; trifler, triflers)

trigger = to start something or set something off; sometimes a switch, button, or lever that makes something happen (trigger, triggers, triggered, triggering)

trim = to make something smaller or shorter; to cut hair or paper; to decorate something or make something be a little better (trim, trims, trimmed, trimming; trimmer, trimmest) 

trousers = a pair of pants; sometimes jeans 

true = right, correct; something that is a fact, not a lie; exact or exactly, real or genuine (true, true, truer, truest; truly; truth, truths)

trump = in a card game one suit of cards (like spades, hearts, diamonds, clubs) more powerful than the other three suits; can mean to do better or be better than something or someone else (trump, trumps, trumped, trumping)

trust = believing in someone or something; expecting you can rely on, or can count on, someone or something (trust, trusts, trusted, trusting; trusty, trustier, trustiest)

tub = a wide, low, usually round container that has a flat bottom and is mostly used for washing things or packing things (tub, tubs; tublike)

tune = a song or melody; can mean to make small changes in something so it works better; can mean adjusting a musical instrument so it plays the right notes (tune, tunes, tuned, tuning; tuner, tuners).

turbid = muddy, thick, hard to see through; can mean confusing (turbid; turbidity) 

turning-point = a time or place when something important changes (turning-point, turning-points)

tyrant = a cruel, unfair leader who has a lot of power (tyrant, tyrants; tyranny; tyrannical)
unabated = not stopping, not slowing down, not getting weaker; still happening just as before 
unaccountable = something that can’t be explained or understood; sometimes means a person can’t be held responsible for something (unaccountable; unaccountably)
unaccustomed = not used to something, not familiar with something 
unbending = someone or something that is very strict, rigid, hard to move or change 

unbounded = without limits, free 

unjust = not fair, not right; usually means someone in power or authority treated someone in a very wrong way (unjust; unjustly)

unknown = not known, unfamiliar; sometimes means a person is anonymous 

unlawful = illegal, against the law; very wrong (unlawful, unlawfully, unlawfulness)

unless = except; something that can’t be without something else happening or being true 

unlike = different; not the same; not equal

unload = to take something away, remove something, or get rid of something (unload, unloads, unloaded, unloading)

unmanageable = hard to handle or control; unruly; difficult to deal with

unmeaning = senseless; without meaning or intelligence; without intending

unmoved = showing or having no feelings; not affected emotionally

unnecessary = something that is not needed; or more than is needed (unnecessary; unnecessarily) 

unpardonable = something that cannot be forgiven, excused, or pardoned (unpardonable) 

unprepared = not ready or able to do something (unprepared; unpreparedness) 

unpunished = a person or action that is not punished, does not receive some a penalty  

unrelenting = not giving up; continuing to try no matter what (unrelenting; unrelentingly) 

unsafe = risky or dangerous (unsafe; unsafely) 

unscriptural = not in agreement with the scriptures, the bible 

unshaken = not bothered, untroubled  

unsuitable = not fitting, not appropriate, should be rejected (unsuitable; unsuitability; unsuitableness) 

until = up to a point in time 

universal = something that affects everyone, is true everywhere (universal; universally)

universe = everything there is; all that exists; all of the galaxies, solar systems, planets, stars, and everything that exists everywhere 

upholder = a person who supports something; especially one who makes a difficult decision to support (uphold, upholds, upheld, upholding; upholder, upholders)

upperground = a piece of land higher up than another piece (upperground, upper-ground)

upward = toward a higher place or position; moving toward a higher place (upward, upwards; upwardly)

urchin= a poor or orphaned child; sometimes a child with no home; sometimes a round sea creature with spikes (urchin, urchins)

urge = a strong feeling, emotion, want, or desire; a sudden impulse; feeling a need do or say something right now (urge, urges, urged, urging; urgent; urgently) 

usher = to lead or guide someone to a seat or to a certain place; a person who shows people where they should be (usher, ushers, ushered, ushering)

utmost = the greatest or highest of something; the most important 

valuable = very important; something that has high value; worth a lot of money (valuable, valuables)

value = how much something is worth, or how important something is (value, values, valued, valuing; valuation)

various = many different kinds (various, varied; variously; variable)

vengeance = to hurt someone because they hurt you; revenge; to want revenge (vengeance)

venture = something risky; to try something knowing it is not safe (venture, ventures, ventured, venturing; venturer, venturers)

verily = an old English word that means ‘truly’ or ‘really’ 

vessel = a ship; sometimes means a container like a jar or bottle (vessel, vessels)

vestige = a trace or small part of something now gone; can mean something no longer useful (vestige, vestiges)

vice = a personal weakness; to behave in a morally weak or evil way (vice, vices)

vicious = to be very mean, cruel, or violent (vicious; viciously; viciousness)

victim = someone hurt or killed by something or by another person, someone who was tricked by someone else (victimize, victimizes, victimized, victimizing; victim, victims) 

view = something to see, usually far away, often pretty; can mean to look at, see, study closely, or think about carefully (view, views, viewed, viewing; viewer, viewers)

vigilant = alert; watching for trouble; being careful (vigilant; vigilance)

village = a small town, usually in the country; can mean the people who live in a small community (village, villages, villager, villagers)

vindicate = to say someone did the right thing; sometimes means to show or prove that someone is innocent and not guilty (vindicate, vindicates, vindicated, vindicating; vindication)

violence = using extremely strong force against a person or property; can mean to try and hurt someone’s body; sometimes means to speak very harshly, or to have and show extremely strong feelings (violent; violence; violently)

virtual = very much like something else; almost exactly like something else; seems almost real (virtual; virtually)

virtue = a kind of moral goodness; good behavior; the right thing to do; can mean a personal value or principle to live by (virtue, virtues; virtuous, virtuously) 	

visible	= something that can be seen (visible; visibly)	

vivid = bright, clear, or powerful; can mean a strong image, something easy to see or remember (vivid, vividly)  

volume = a book; sometimes means how much space something takes up or occupies; can mean the amount of something (volume, volumes; voluminous) 

voluntary = to do something without being told to do it; to freely choose to do something; to choose to do something without any reward or pay (voluntary; voluntarily)

volunteer = freely choose to do something without pressure from anyone; sometimes means to do something while expecting nothing in return (volunteer, volunteers, volunteered, volunteering)

vow = a promise; to make a strong, serious promise (vow, vows, vowed, vowing)

wage = money paid to someone for work (wage, wages)

wakefulness = not sleeping; not being able to sleep; sleeplessness; sometimes means to be alert, watching or waiting for something, vigilant (wakeful, wakefulness)

wake = to stop sleeping (wake, wakes, woke, awakened, waking)
 
wall = a part of a building that holds up the roof or that divides rooms; can mean a kind of fence made of stones or bricks; sometimes means to separate one place or one thing from another (wall, walls, walled, walling; wall-like)

wallow = to roll around in mud or water (wallow, wallows, wallowed, wallowing).

warehouse =	a place to store or keep things in; often a large building (warehouse, warehouses)	

warm-hearted = kind, generous, sympathetic, comforting (warm-hearted, warmhearted, warmheartedness, warmly)

warrant = a document allowing the police to arrest someone or to search property; can mean a reason or doing something; to say ‘I warrant’ can mean ‘I believe’  (warrant, warrants, warranted, warranting)

waste = can mean to spend carelessly, or make something lose value; something thrown away, garbage; can mean empty or deserted land; sometimes means loss through use or misuse or decay (waste, wastes, wasted, wasting)

watch = to keep looking, to be observant; can mean to take care of; or to be careful, on guard; can mean a small clock worn like a bracelet (watch, watches, watched, watching; watchful; watcher; watchman)

watchword = a kind of password or phrase used by members of a group; can mean a kind of guideline

way = how to go or proceed; a possible path to progress or complete a task; a direction; can mean a manner of thinking (way, ways)

weak = not being strong, loud, or energetic; easy to defeat or overcome (weak, weaker, weakest; weakly; weakness; weakling)

weaken = to become less strong, or to work less well (weaken, weakens, weakened, weakening)

weary = tired; to have lost strength, ability, or interest (weary, wearies, wearied, wearying; wearier, weariest)

weather = what it’s like outside: windy, rainy, stormy, snowy, hot, cold, etc.; can mean how something changes because of too much sun or being rained on; can mean how well someone does in bad situations (weather, weathers, weathered, weathering)

weave = to make by lacing or crossing threads to make cloth, or slender sticks sideways and up-and-down to make a basket; can mean a person or animal moving in and out, back and forth, up and down (weave, weaves, wove, woven, weaving; weaver, weavers)

week = 7 days, often means Monday through Sunday; a normal workweek is 5 days Monday through Friday; weekly usually means something happens once a week (week, weeks; weekly; workweek)

weigh = to find out how heavy something or someone is; the weight of something is how much it weighs; can mean to consider possible options (weigh, weighs, weighed, weighing; weight, weights)

welcome = to greet in a friendly way; can mean to accept something gladly (welcome, welcomes, welcomed, welcoming)

welfare – being well or doing well, especially in terms of happiness, living conditions, or success; sometimes a person’s well-being or mental state; can mean providing money or help to people in need 

well-trained = having had good instruction and experience; being able to do well at a job or task
 
west = the direction where the sun sets; on a map usually the left side; can mean places or countries in that direction (west; westerly; western) 

wharf = a structure on land where large ships in a harbor pick up and unload cargo (wharf, wharfs, wharves)

whence = from this place; can mean a place where something started; can mean the ideas or reasons someone decides or concludes something 

whereabouts = close to a location where someone or something happened or was or can be found; can mean ‘around here’ or ‘around there’

whereas = can mean ‘since it is true that’; or can mean ‘while just the opposite is true’ [cold turns water to ice, whereas heat turns water to steam] 

whereby = because of this, or through this; can mean ‘how’

whether = meaning ‘if it was or is true that’ or ‘if it was or is better that’; can mean either of two things can be true:  I eat ice cream whether I’m hungry or not.
whichever = any of these; whatever 

whip–scarred= skin marked with scars from beatings or other forms of abuse

whipping-post = a piece of wood or metal where people are tied to be whipped (whipping-post)

whisky = a strong alcoholic drink, a type of liquor (whiskey, whiskeys)

wide = broad; a large measure across or sideways; a large space; can mean fully open (wide, wider, widest; widely)

wild = not tame; not under control or restrained; in natural state, not influenced by humans (wild, wilder, wildest; wildly)

wit = ability to think, especially to think quickly, and to say something clever and amusing or funny (wit, wits; witty, wittier, wittiest)

withhold = to keep and not give; to refuse to give or allow something (withhold, withholds, withheld, withholding)

within = in or inside; into

woe = great sadness, sorrow, grief, trouble; woeful means full of regret and sadness (woe, woes; woeful; woefully)

wood-fence = a wooden structure that surrounds or blocks off something 

wood-horse = an old-fashioned word for a ship; can mean a type of cane to help someone walk; can mean a torture device; can mean a trick:  in one old story soldiers hid inside a ‘wooden horse’ to sneak inside a city (wood-horse, wooden horse)

workman = a person who works for a living; sometimes means a skilled worker like a carpenter or painter or welder

worship = to show honor to a higher power like God or some holy object; to give religious praise; sometimes means to praise or believe too much (worship, worships, worshipped, worshipping; worshipper, worshiper, worshippers, worshipers)

worth = value or usefulness; sometimes the cost of something; sometimes can mean excellence; to be ‘worthy’ is to have value or excellence (worth; worthy)

wretched = to be very sick, injured, poor, or in misery; can mean awful behavior (wretched; wretchedly; wretchedness; wretch, wretches) 

wrong = incorrect; not right; unfair; improper; can mean not lawful; can mean injuries or harmful things done to someone (wrong, wrongs, wronged, wronging)

yard = a unit of measurement of 36 inches or three feet, about as long as one big step; can mean large outdoor area, often a grassy space in front of or behind a home; can mean a long pole that holds up and spreads a sail on a ship (yard, yards)

yearly = something that happens once a year, every 12 months

yoke = a wood bar to join two working animals who pull a wagon or plow; can mean to tie or hook or join together; can mean something that causes pain, suffering, or lack of freedom (yoke, yokes, yoked, yoking)

youth = can mean childhood, or sometimes the period between childhood and becoming an adult; not mature (youth; youths, youthful; youthfulness)

accident = something not supposed to happen; an unplanned event or situation; often means some unexpected event that causes damage (accident, accidents; accidental; accidentally)
accompany = to go with or belong with someone or something; an ‘accompaniment’ is a musical part that supports a song, or can mean an addition that completes something (accompany, accompanies, accompanied, accompanying; accompaniment)

account = a record of money received and spent; can mean a report of something that happened, or to explain reasons and causes for something(account, accounts, accounted, accounting)
accouterments = can mean what someone wears or brings, especially for some special activity; can mean extra clothing or equipment; sometimes means a soldier’s special equipment (accouterment, accouterments)

accusative = an accusing tone of voice; finding fault or blaming someone (accusative; accusatory; accusatorial)
acknowledge = to accept, admit or recognize; can mean to thank or praise someone for some achievement or for doing something well (acknowledge, acknowledges, acknowledged, acknowledging; acknowledgment) 
acme = a high point; sometimes means the highest degree of perfection

acre = an area of land, about half of a football field or soccer field; a land measurement often used by farmers (acre, acres; acreage)
acrobat = a gymnast; someone who is good at leaps, tumbles, flips, and other acrobatic activities; can sometimes mean; someone who quickly changes ideas or viewpoints (acrobat, acrobats; acrobatic; acrobatics; acrobatically)
across = from one side or position to another; can mean something crossed, or something on the opposite side from something else 
acute = something sharp and pointed; ca mean something hard, difficult, or severe; can mean especially sensitive; sometimes means especially intelligent, quick witted, or shrewd (acute, acuter, acutest; acutely; acuteness)

adventure = an exciting, sometimes dangerous, experience or activity (adventure, adventures, adventured, adventuring)

advisable = something that would be recommended (advisable; advisably)

afar = at a distance or to a distance; a long way off 
affable = friendly, pleasant, good-humored, easy to talk to (affable; affably)

agape = to the mouth wide open, often because of shock, surprise, or wonder

agility = the ability to move, think, or understand quickly, easily, and well (agility; agilities)

ahem = a word for the noise made when someone clears the throat, often to attract attention, sometimes to show dislike or embarrassment  (ahem, hem)
aide = someone who helps; sometimes a caregiver for someone ill or injured; sometimes an assistant to an important person (aide, aides)
ail = to feel troubled, sometimes with physical illness, sometimes emotionally as with with fear, dread, or worry; an ‘ailment’ is sometimes a minor illness (ail, ails, ailed, ailing; ailment) 
aimless = without a purpose, reason, or direction (aimless; aimlessly; aimlessness) 
air = what we breathe and what wind is; an invisible gas mostly oxygen and nitrogen; to ‘put on airs’ is to act better or more important than you are; people who ‘have an air’ create a special impression (air, airs)

alert = quick to notice, especially something unusual or dangerous; also means able to think clearly; can mean watching carefully for danger or trouble, or to warn someone (alert, alerts, alerted, alerting) 
align = to place things in a straight line, or in correct positions; to bring people into agreement (align, aligns, aligned, aligning; alignment) 
alive =  a person, animal, or plant being living, not dead; can also mean alert and active; sometimes means aware of or interested in something 
allay = to put at rest, or to become less, as with fear or worry; can mean to reduce or relieve some unpleasant feeling such as pain or hunger (allay, allays, allayed, allaying) 
allegiance = loyalty or commitment to something or someone, as when school children pledge allegiance to the flag 
allure = to attract; charm, or tempt; to fascinate and spark desire; ‘allurements’ are attractive qualities, traits, or behaviors, especially those which are mysterious or forbidden (allure, allures, allured, alluring; alluringly; allurement, allurements) 
allusion = to suggest or refer to something without mentioning it directly, often a name, fact, or phrase (allusion, allusions) 
almond = the nutlike seed of the almond tree, oval shaped and flavorful (almond, almonds) 
alone = apart from anyone; without another person; having no companion or companions 
along = moving in a constant direction, often beside something; sometimes means making progress or the passage of time; ‘along with’ can mean being in the company of others
aloud = speaking in a way that can be heard, not silent or whispered 
already = before now; sometimes means ‘this’ time; often spelled ‘all ready’
altar = a table, flat-topped block, or other object used as a focal point in religious practices; often associated with a priest or priestess; not the same word as ‘alter’ which means to change (altar, altars)
altercation = a noisy, often public, argument or disagreement; can mean a fight (altercation, altercations)
alter = to change or cause change in something, often a small but important change; the change would be an ‘alteration’; not the same word as ‘alter’ which means a religious object (alter, alters, altered, altering; alteration, alterations) 
alternate = an AL-ternate is a person or thing which acts as a substitute or takes the place of another; to AL-ter-NATE is to occur every other time, as numbers alternate between even and odd (alternate, alternates, alternated, alternating; alternately) 
although = even though, or even if, or in spite of the fact; sometimes means ‘however’ 
altogether = wholly; completely; can mean including everything or everyone; can also mean taking everything into consideration 
amateur = people not paid for what they do; not a professional; sometimes means sa person who lacks a high level of skill, or to describe something done poorly or with little skill (amateur, amateurs; amateurish)
amaze = to surprise someone greatly; to create a sense of wonder (amaze, amazes, amazed, amazing; amazingly; amazement)
amber = a hard yellow, orange, or red substance that exists as a fossil created by tree sap; can also refer to a honey-yellow color; often used to make jewelry; can be a girl’s name; ‘amber-tinted’ means amber colored  
amble = to move smoothly and easily; to walk or move at a slow, relaxed pace (amble, ambles, ambled, ambling; ambler, amblers) 
amiable = likeable; good-natured; having a friendly and pleasant manner (amiable; amiably; amiableness) 
amicable = having a friendly personality; pleasant and agreeable (amicable; amicably; amicableness) 
amiss = not quite right, or out of place; improper; faulty; wrong or wrongly 
ammunition = a supply of weapons that can be shot or projected, such as bullets, bombs, missiles; sometimes means other weapons, sometimes thoughts or facts to support an argument 
ample = enough, or more than enough (ample, amply)

ancient = very old; having existed for a very long time; sometimes means from a very strange and different time long ago

anger = a strong feeling of extreme irritation or dislike; can mean to cause someone to feel angry (anger, angers, angered, angering; angrily) 
animal = a living creature that eats, can move around, and makes new versions of itself such as children (animal, animals; animal-like)

blue-clothed = wearing blue clothes or uniforms; during the Civil War the Union soldiers mostly wore blue, the Confederate or rebel soldiers mostly wore gray

blue-grass = a grass which sometimes had a light blue tint; grass mostly associated with Kentucky; now a term for one kind of country music (blue-grass, bluegrass) 

blue-point = a small oyster, usually served raw (bluepoint, bluepoints, blue-point, blue-points)

blunder = a careless mistake; clumsy, awkward, stumbling behavior (blunder, blunders, blundered, blundering)

blur = to smear, blot, or smudge; to become hard to see, remember, or understand; when things run together or become confused (blur, blurs, blurred, blurring)

blurt = to speak suddenly without thinking; to speak in a rush, thoughtlessly and impulsively (blurt, blurts, blurted, blurting)

bluster = wind blowing strongly as in a storm; can mean to speak noisily and energetically, to show off or make loud threats (bluster, blusters, blustered, blustering; blustery)

board = a thin, flat piece of wood used for construction; can mean to go onto a ship; ‘room and board’ means to pay for a room and meals; a ‘board’ might be a group of people who oversee or control an organization (board, boards, boarded, boarding)

boast = to brag; to talk, especially about yourself, with excessive pride; to exaggerate    (boast, boasts, boasted, boasting; boastful)

boat = a small open vehicle used on the water; sometimes also used larger water vehicles such as ships (boat, boats)

bob = to move up and down; can mean to cut hair or an animal’s tail; also a nickname for Robert (bob, bobs, bobbed, bobbing)

bodice = the upper part of woman’s dress (bodice, bodices)

bold = brave, courageous, willing to take risks (bold, bolder, boldest; boldness)

bolt = a thick metal screw; a sliding lock for a door; a flash of thunder and lightning; a thick arrow shot from a crossbow; can also mean to move or jump quickly; or to quickly leave  (bolt, bolts, bolted, bolting)

bombast = boastful or overly proud; vain, pompous talk (bombast; bombastic)

bonbon = candy with a fruit, nut, or cream filling (bonbon, bonbons, bon-bon, bon-bons)

bone-crushing = something extremely painful; something that can cause serious injury

bonfire = a large, outdoor fire, often for people to gather around (bonfire, bonfires, bon-fire, bon-fires)

bonnet = a woman’s cloth hat without a brim, often fastened by tying a string under the chin, sometimes very colorful and fancy; a feathered headdress sometimes worn as a mark of honor by American Indians (bonnet, bonnets)

booby = a foolish person; also the name of a seabird

bookshelf = a shelf made to store books, but often used to display pictures, small objects, knickknacks  (bookshelf, bookshelves, book-shelf, book-shelves)

boom = a loud, explosive sound; sometimes describes a sudden increase of business, political support, or in some other activity; sometimes a long pole to rig sails on a ship’s mast, or to support things from a derrick or tower (boom, booms, boomed, booming)

boon = a fine gift, favor, blessing, or honor; something helpful or that benefits someone; can mean a very good friend, someone kind, generous, friendly, trustworthy (boon, boons)

bore = to make a hole; also means someone or something that is monotonous, not interesting, fun, or exciting; can mean to cause people to feel dull, tired, weary, uneasy   (bore, bores, bored, boring; boredom)

orrow = to take something, usually with a promise to return or replace it (borrows, borrowed, borrowing)

bottle = a round container with no handles, often with a cap or lid on top, usually made to hold liquids; can mean to block any exit so that people or animals cannot get out  (bottle, bottles, bottled, bottling)

bough = a large branch on a tree, usually a thick main branch (bough, boughs)

bouillon = clear soup broth

bound = to leap or jump or bounce high and far; can also mean tied; can mean closely connected or devoted to something or someone; sometimes means a limit or border (bound, bounds, bounded, bounding)

bounty = having a lot of something good; generosity; can mean a promised reward for something (bounty, bounties; bountiful)

bouquet = a group of flowers, often specially arranged; sometimes means an aroma or fragrance, especially for wine (bouquet, bouquets)

bourgeois = associate with middle class, between the rich and the poor; often means conservative, respectable, commonplace, ordinary, smug (bourgeois; bourgeoisie)

boulder = a very large rock, too heavy to lift (boulder, boulders, bowlder, bowlders)

boy = a young male, not yet a man (boy, boys; boyhood; boyish)

break = to cause something to come apart into pieces, to damage or destroy something; can mean to interrupt or end something (break, breaks, broke, breaking; can broken)

breast = the front of the body between the neck and stomach; the chest area; can mean soldiers coming through or over the enemy defense line (breast, breasts, breasted, breasting)

breathe = to inhale and exhale, take air into the lungs and blow it out; can mean to be alive; can mean to take a short rest (breathe, breathes, breathed, breathing)

broken-bladed = a youthful fantasy of heroics on a battlefield among broken swords, knives, bayonets

broker = someone whose business is to buy and sell valuable stocks and bonds, or sometimes great quantities of goods like wheat, corn, cotton, tobacco (broker, brokers; brokerage)

bronze = a metal made from a blend of copper and tin, normally a bright yellow or golden orange color (bronze, bronzed)

brood = when a bird sits on eggs to hatch them; can mean young animals or children, or to watch over and protect them; sometimes mean a person continually thinking deep thoughts about something troubling (brood, broods, brooded, brooding)

brotherly = to show kindness, affection, or loyalty to another

brotherhood = a warm and close connection among a group of men; can mean kindness, affection, or loyalty between brothers or people who feel like they are family (brotherhood; brotherly)

brown = the color that comes when you mix red, yellow, and black, sometimes a lighter color, sometimes darker; can mean to lightly cook red meat until it becomes dry and hard (brown, browns, browned, browning; brownish)

browse = to leisurely look through and sample a book or other text; can mean when animals like sheep, cattle, or deer slowly nibble and eat their way across a field of grass, bushes, and other plants  (browse, browses, browsed, browsing)

brush = to lightly touch or move across; can mean to clean, tidy, or straighten by moving a tool with hair-like bristles across a surface; sometimes the name for the tool with hair-like bristles (brush, brushes, brushed, brushing)

budge = to cause something to move just a little (budge, budges, budged, budging)

bud = a new part of a plant, or to begin to grow a new part of a plant, such as a flower or a leaf; sometimes means to be young and to begin on the path to become mature (bud, buds, budded, budding)

buffalo = a large animal similar to a cow; sometimes a bison; sometimes to ‘buffalo’ means to fool or overwhelm or bully or intimidate someone (buffalo, buffaloes, buffaloed, buffalowing)

buff = to clean or polish (buff, buffs, buffed, buffing)

buffet = a bu-FFET is a piece of furniture with drawers, cupboards, and space for many plates; or a meal where people walk beside a table with many foods and fill their plates; to BUFF-et is to hit, punch, or slap (buffet, buffets, buffeted, buffeting) 
buggy = a small carriage, normally for two riders, which usually had two wheels and was pulled by one horse, though sometimes four wheels and more riders; also means a wheeled device pushed by an adult for a baby to ride(buggies)

bulge = to swell or bend outward (bulge, bulges, bulged, bulging)

bulky = something that takes up a lot of space, but is usually not heavy (bulky, bulkier, bulkiest)

cabin = a small house that is built in a very simple way, sometimes with logs (cabin, cabins)

capable = able to do something (capable; capability, capabilities)

cigarette = a short, narrow tube of paper filled with tobacco for smoking; a cigar is similar, but longer and fatter, tightly rolled, and without the paper covering (cigarette, cigarettes, cigar, cigars)

circlet = a small circle; can mean a circular piece of jewelry worn on the head (circlet, circlets)

circle = a perfectly round shape; can mean to surround something, or to go all the way around (circle, circles, circled, circling)

circus-men = men who travel with a circus, sometimes acrobats or animal trainers, sometimes ‘roustabouts’ who put up tents and take care of animals 

cistern = a large underground container, sometimes made of stone, brick or metal,  designed for catching and storing water, especially rainwater (cistern, cisterns)

cite = to use someone else’s words; to quote someone giving that first person credit, especially when writing (cite, cites; citation)

civil = having to do with people, a citizen or citizens in a community or society; or having to do with government; sometimes means to be polite, to have good manners, to be courteous, to behave in a civilized way (civil, civility)

clad = wearing something

clamber = to climb in an awkward, clumsy way; to move awkwardly using hands and feet (clamber, clambers, clambered, clambering)

clammy = unpleasantly, moist or cold, sometimes sticky (clammy, clammier, clammiest)

clamor = loud noise that goes on for a long time; sometimes means a demand or complaint (clamor, clamors, clamored, clamoring; clamorings) 

clang = to make a loud, clear sound or ring, often make by hitting metal; sometimes a sound made by a bell or an alarm (clang, clangs, clanged, clanging; clangor, clangour)

clank = the short sound of metal being hit (clank, clanks, clanked, clanking)

clan = a large group of people with a lot in common, sometimes members of a large, extended family, sometimes people sharing common interests (clan, clans; clannish; clannishly)

clap = to strike two things together to make a sharp sound (clap, claps, clapped, clapping; clapper, clappers)

claret = a red table wine, not very sweet; can mean a purplish red color (claret, clarets)

clash = to collide; often means to suddenly slam together making a loud sound; can mean to disagree or to fight; can mean two things that don’t fit well together, such as colors or personalities or articles of clothing  (clash, clashes, clashed, clashing)

clasp = to hold onto; to hold, hug, or embrace strongly; sometimes a device with two pinchers that hold things together like the two ends of a necklace or bracelet (clasp, clasps, clasped, clasping)

classic = something that remains very popular for a long time; something of high and lasting quality; can mean something very special; can mean something from ancient Greek or Roman culture  (classic, classics; classical; classically)

clatter = to make a loud rattling noise (clatter, clatters, clattered, clattering)

clawlike = something that looks like a claw; often means thin fingers with long fingernails, or pawlike with long pointed tips or pinchers  (clawlike, claw-like)

clean-shaved = without whiskers on the cheeks or chin; to have facial hair shaved off

clear-headedness = to have good perception, awareness, and understanding 

clear = free from darkness or clouds, free from confusion; can mean clouds or smoke going away; can mean to cut down bushes and trees on a piece of land (clear, clears, cleared, clearing; clearness, clarity)

clematis = a climbing plant with bright colored flowers

clementine = a tangerine, like an orange but a little smaller; at one time a girl’s name (clementine, clementines)

clergyman = a religious leader; someone who leads a religious group or performs religious ceremonies (clergyman, clergymen)

clever = very intelligent, quick to learn; skillful; sometimes means quick-witted or tricky (clever, cleverer, cleverest; cleverly; cleverness)

click = a slight sharp sound; clickety-click is a fast rhythmic clicking sound like train wheels moving across rails (click, clicks, clicked, clicking; clickety-click)

cliff = a high, rocky place that sticks out over lots of empty space (cliff, cliffs)

clinch = to hold tight or fasten together; can mean a firm hug or embrace; can mean to settle an argument or come to an agreement; can mean when boxers or wrestlers grasp each other and won’t let go (clinch, clinches, clinched, clinching; clincher)

clip = to make a short, simple cut; to trim just a little, or something trimmed off; can mean to fasten to something, or something that fastens (clip, clips, clipped, clipping; clipper)

cloak = something to be worn loose on the back, usually without sleeves; can mean to cover or hide or disguise (cloak, cloaks, cloaked, cloaking)

clod = a rough lump of earth or clay; sometimes means someone not very smart or with poor social skills  (clod, clods; cloddish)

clog = to block something, prevent something from passing through; can mean something that blocks or hinders movement; sometimes a name for a heavy shoe, often made of wood, or a kind of dance using those shoes (clog, clogs, clogged, clogging)

close = clo-S-e means near; not far away; clo-Z-e means to shut something (close, closer, closest; close, closed, closes, closing)

cloth = a woven or knitted fabric made of cotton, wool, silk, or similar material; can mean a piece of fabric used to make shirts, pants, sheets, curtains, and other objects

clothe = to dress; to wear garments or put them on someone; can mean the garments to be worn (clothe, clothes, clothed, clothing)

cloud = white or gray masses in the sky made of tiny water droplets; where rain and lightning come from; can mean a mass of smoke, dust, or steam visible in the air; can mean to make dark, gloomy, or troubled (cloud, clouds, clouded, clouding; cloudy)

club = a heavy wooden stick, usually thicker at one end,  used as a weapon; can mean to hit or beat with a heavy object; can also mean an organization or social group people join; can mean place to gather socially, or to party (club, clubs, clubbed, clubbing)

cluck = the sound a chicken makes, especially a hen (cluck, clucks, clucked, clucking)

clump = a group of things close to each other; can mean to bring or put things together; can mean a disordered bunch of things (clump, clumps, clumped, clumping)

clumsy = awkward, without grace, skill, or control; can mean badly shaped or poorly put together (clumsy, clumsier, clumsiest; clumsily)

cling = to hold onto something as if afraid to let go; to barely grasp or hold on; to hold tightly (cling, clings, clung, clinging; clingy)

cluster = a small group of things that are alike; to grow or gather together in a small group (cluster, clusters, clustered, clustering)

clutch = to grab, snatch, or hold onto something; a grasp or grip tightly; sometimes means a nest of eggs, or group of baby chickens; sometimes means a purse or handbag without straps or a handle (clutch, clutches, clutched, clutching)

clutter = make messy, disordered, or jumbled; to litter; filled with too much stuff (clutter, clutters, cluttered, cluttering)

coachman = someone who drives and controls the horses who pull a coach or carriage (coachman, coachmen, coach-driver)  [duplicates ‘coach-driver]

coast = seashore, the land next to an ocean; can mean to sail a ship not far from shore; can also mean to keep going on without using energy, as on a sled or wagon going downhill (coast, coasts, coasted, coasting)

coat = a warm garment worn over the clothes; can mean the outer skin and fur of an animal; also means to add a layer of something such as paint (coat, coats, coated, coating)

coax = to gently convince or encourage someone to do something (coax, coaxes, coaxed, coaxing)

cocktail = an alcoholic mixed drink (cocktail, cocktails)

coconut = the large, brown seed of a palm tree; also means the sweet tasting white fruit found inside the shell (coconut, coconuts, cocoanut, cocoanuts) 

coddle = to pamper someone, give then whatever they want; to treat someone like a baby (coddle, coddles, coddling, coddled)

code = a set of rules or set of principles; sometimes to send messages, especially secret messages using special symbols, letters, or numbers; can mean the , key to get into a secret or private system (code, codes, coded, coding)

coerce = to pressure, threaten, force, or compel someone to do something they don’t want to do (coerce, coerces, coerced, coercing; coercion)

coffee-cup = a cup or mug for holding hot drinks like coffee or tea (coffee-cup, coffee-cups; coffee-mug, coffee-mugs) 

cohere = to hold together; to be connected (cohere, coheres, cohered, cohering) 

coherent = something that holds together, is logically connected, or makes sense (coherent, coherence)


coldly = to act in a way that is detached or unkind; to show a lack of concern, caring, or affection (coldly, coldness)

collapse = to fall down or fall in; sometimes to fold or push something in; to suddenly break down; to fail; sometimes to become very sick or ill  (collapse, collapsed, collapses, collapsing)

collection = a group of closely related/the same kinds of things (collections)

collective = a group unified by some idea, principle, or goal; people who work, do something, or own something as a group (collective, collectively)

college = a school that you can go to after high school; an association or formal group of people who have certain powers, rights, and duties; with a shared goal or purpose

color = a hue like red or green or blue; can mean to change a tint or hue by using paint, crayons, pigment, or dye;  can mean to have or add emphasis or interest to something (color, colors, colored, coloring)

colossal = gigantic, enormous, extremely large

column = a pillar or pole, usually tall, thin and round, to supports a roof or for decoration; can mean a row of lines of printed text, or a regular article or essay in a newspaper; can mean soldiers organized in a line (column, columns, columnlike)

combat = a COM-bat is a fight or struggle; to com-BAT is to be fighting or struggling; a ‘combatant’ is a fighter;  to be ‘combative’ is to like or be eager to fight  (combat, combats, combatted, combating; combatant, combatants; combative)

comedy = a play, book, or show that is funny or silly and that has a happy ending; a ‘comedian’ makes people laugh, often by telling jokes (comedy, comedies; comedian, comedians)

comic = funny, silly, something to amuse people or make them laugh; sometimes a type of cartoon published in a newspaper or as a book; sometimes a comedian who tells jokes or does things to make people laugh (comic, comics; comical)

commander = a person who leads or controls, especially in the military (commander, commanders)

commend = to praise someone for doing something; can mean to put someone or something under the care of someone (commend, commends, commended, commending; commendable)

comment = to say something, remark, give an opinion, provide feedback; sometimes to criticize or to gossip (comment, comments, commented, commenting)

commiserate = to feel or express sympathy, sorrow, or pity; to feel sorry for someone sad or in trouble (commiserate, commiserates, commiserated, commiserating; commiseration)

commodious = comfortably spacious, roomy

commonplace = ordinary; usual, no new or interesting; can mean an obvious remark, often heard, boring (commonplace, commonplaces)

commotion = noisy confusion, chaos, turmoil, or disorder (commotion, commotions)

commune = to com-MUNE is to be in close or very friendly communication with a person or with nature; can mean to share close or intimate feelings; a COM-mune is where a group of people can live in a shared space (commune, communes, communed, communing)

compact = com-PACT means firmly packed together; to COM-pact is to pack things together firmly (compact, compacts, compacted, compacting; compactor)

companionable = friendly, easy to travel or associate with, sociable, warm and easy going

comparative = can mean similar to; or can be compared to something else or relative to something else (comparative; comparatively; comparison)

compartment = an area or part of something that is separated off; sometimes a separate room or part of a room; sometimes a special place in a larger container like a toolbox or purse (compartment, compartments)

compass = a round device with a dial that always points north; used for finding directions; or an angled device for making circles; to ‘compass’ can mean to go around or to surround something (compass, compasses, compassed, compassing) 

competent = able to do something; capable; sufficient; adequate (competent; competence, competency)

complacent = satisfied, especially with yourself or your situation; having no desire to change (complacent, complacency)
   
complete = whole; entire; thorough; can mean finished, or to finish something (complete, completes, completed, completing; completely

complex = com-PLEX means complicated; a COM-plex can be several things linked together, such as a business complex; can sometimes mean a psychological problem   (complex, complexes; complexities)

complicate = to make things more difficult to do or to understand (complicate, complicates, complicated, complicating; complications)

compliment = to praise someone, or show someone your approval (compliment, compliments, complimented, complimenting)

composite = made up of two or more parts, often several parts (composite, composites) 

composure = a state of calmness in action or thought; controlled emotions

comprehend = to understand something, especially something difficult; can also mean to include something (comprehend, comprehends, comprehended, comprehending; comprehension)

comprehensive = including everything relevant; not leaving anything out  (comprehensive; comprehensively)

comprise = to include or contain; can mean to consist of, to be composed of, or to be made up of (comprise, comprises, comprised, comprising)

compulsion = being forced to do something; being made to act against your will; sometimes means an irresistible impulse, feeling an emotion drive that can’t be resisted (compulsion; compulsive; compulsively; compulsory)

compunction = to feel bad, uneasy, or unsure about doing something; worry that  something should not be done; concern over the rightness of an action; to feel regret for doing something wrong (compunction, compunctions)

comrade = a close friend, associate, or companion; someone you spend time with and with whom you share important interests (comrade, comrades; comradeship; comradely)

conceit = an exaggerated opinion about how good, important, wonderful you are; excessive pride; vanity; sometimes a ‘conceit’ is to say something witty, imaginative, or poetic; in olden times it meant a comparison or an idea (conceit; conceits; conceited)

conceivable = something that can be thought, imagined, understood, or believed (conceivable; conceivably)

conciliate = to make peace; to soothe someone, placate them, or win them over; to create good will (conciliate, conciliates, conciliated, conciliating; conciliation; conciliatory)

concoct = to make by putting several ingredients together; sometimes to create an imaginative story or develop a wild plan (concoct, concocts, concocted, concocting; concoction)

concussion = violent shaking or shock from a smashing impact; a violent shaking or a hard hit; can mean an injury to the brain caused by a violent blow or powerful impact (concussion; concussions)

condemn = to strongly disapprove; to convict or declare guilty of crime or wrongdoing; to reject something as wrong or evil (condemn, condemns, condemned, condemning; condemnation)

condescend = to act superior to or better than someone or something; to treat someone or something with little or no respect (condescend, condescends, condescended, condescending; condescension)

confection = candy, bonbons, ice cream or some other sweet treat (confection, confections; confectioner, confectioners)

confederate = someone united with others in a loose organization supporting a common cause or goal; a close companion; can mean an associate in crime, an accomplice; a Southern soldier during the Civil War (confederate, confederates; confederacy)

conference = a meeting to discuss a particular topic; to hold or to be present at a meeting (conference, conferences, conferenced, conferencing)

confess = to admit doing something wrong; can mean to express faith in something; in some religions to acknowledge sins to a priest and ask for forgiveness (confess, confesses, confessed, confessing; confession, confessions)

confidant = a person someone has faith in, trusts, and shares secrets with (confidant, confidants) 

confidential = private or secret; information not to be shared with others (confidential, confidentially)

confirm = to prove or show something is true, real, or to be trusted; can mean to approve or accept someone or something (confirm, confirms, confirmed, confirming; confirmation)

confirmatory = showing or giving evidence that something is true, accurate, or right

conflict = to con-FLICT is to disagree or differ or to fight; a CON-flict is a disagreement or a fight  (conflict, conflicts, conflicted, conflicting)

confront = to face someone or something, especially when there is some conflict; can mean to accuse or to face fearlessly (confront, confronts, confronted, confronting; confrontation)

confuse = to cause misunderstanding; or to mix up mentally; to jumble or bewilder; can mean to mistake one thing for another (confuse, confuses, confused, confusing; confusion)

congenial = friendly, agreeable, compatible; easy to get along with (congenial; congenially; congeniality)

conger = a large salt-water eel; an fish that looks like a snake

congratulate = to tell someone you’re happy for their achievement or success (congratulate, congratulates, congratulated, congratulating; congratulation, congratulations)

congregation = a gathering of people or things; people assembled for a meeting or for  religious worship 

conjure = to make something or someone appear by magic; to practice magic (conjure, conjures, conjured, conjuring; conjuror, conjurors)

conquer = to defeat, especially in battle; to win; to overcome (conquer, conquers, conquered, conquering; conqueror, conquerors; conquest)

conscious = aware, especially of surroundings and what is going on; able to think and feel; having thoughts, feelings, and impressions (conscious; consciously; consciousness)

consecutive = following in order; occurring in a series, one after the other; proceeding in a logical order (consecutive; consecutively) 

consign = to send, deliver, or hand over; can mean to have someone take charge of something (consign, consigns, consigned, consigning; consignment)

consternation = strong upset, dismay, amazement, or terror

constitute = to make or to set up something; can mean to establish a law, or initiate an assembly (constitute, constitutes, constituted, constituting)

constitutional = having to do with a constitution, such as the basic laws of a government; an old fashioned word for taking a walk to improve someone’s health or ‘constitution’

consul = a government official who lives in a foreign country and oversees the welfare of his fellow citizens in that country; also a term for political leaders in ancient Rome (consul, consuls; consulate)

contact = when two people or things touch, meet, or exchange information; can mean when someone communicates with another person (contact, contacts, contacted, contacting)

contagion = something bad spread from person to person, often a disease or bad idea or bad behavior (contagion; contagious)

contemplation = thinking about, studying, or considering something; often means to have deep, serious thoughts; to meditate about something (contemplation, contemplative)

contemporary = at the same time period as something else; can mean an object or person that belongs to the same generation or century; can refer to how things are now 
(contemporary, contemporaries; contemporaneous, contemporaneously)

contempt = scorn; disdain; feeling that something is low, unworthy, disgusting, should  be despised (contempt; contemptible; contemptuous; contemptuously)

continent = a huge mass of land, like all of North America or of Africa; one of the seven major areas of land on earth (continent, continents)

continual = to go on without stopping (continual, continually; continuous, continuously; continuity)

contort = to twist or bend something, especially in an awkward way or shape; to wrench, distort, or force out of shape (contort, contorts, contorted, contorting;  contortion, contortions; contortionist)

contradict = to oppose, deny, or disagree; to be against something; to be contrary; can mean for someone to deny or say the opposite of what they said before (contradict, contradicts, contradicted, contradicting; contradictory; contradiction, contradictions)

contrast = a CON-trast is the difference between one thing and another;to con-TRAST is to compare in order to identify or understand differences (contrast, contrasts, contrasted, contrasting)

contrive = to create something; to plan, invent, design, or devise; can mean to scheme in a bad way (contrive, contrives, contrived, contriving; contrivance, contrivances)

controversy = something many people disagree, debate, or argue about (controversy, controversies; controversial)

convenience = to be useful or handy (conveniences)

convenient = useful or handy, easy and helpful; easily accessible (convenient; convenience, conveniences)

convey = to deliver something, or to make something known, or to transfer something (convey, conveys, conveyed, conveying; conveyance; conveyer, conveyers) 

convolvulus-runners = the long stems of some plants with trumpet shaped flowers, like morning glory plants

convulse = to shake uncontrollably; to agitate or disturb violently; can mean to bend over or shake with emotion such as laughter or anger (convulse, convulses, convulsed, convulsing; convulsion, convulsions; convulsive; convulsively)

cookbook = a collection of recipes, directions for making food (cookbook; cookbooks)

cooking-smells = scents and odors created when preparing food

cool = less than cold; can mean to make less warm; often a pleasant feeling in warm weather; can mean not excited, unemotional; indifferent, not caring much (cool, cools, cooled, cooling; coolness; coolly)

cope = to deal with or to handle something; can sometimes mean to fight without losing (cope, copes, coped, coping)

copper = a reddish brown metal, often used to make coins like pennies; in slang sometimes means a policeman (copper; coppers)

coquette = a girl or woman who flirts excessively; can mean to flirt or to trifle with (coquet, coquette, coquettes, coquetted, coquetting; coquettish; coquettishly; coquettishness; coquetry, coquetries)

coral = the hard skeleton of tiny sea animals; can mean reefs of big rock-like underwater structures created by the skeletons; can mean an orange-pink color (coral, corals, coral-reef, coral-reefs)

Corinthian = a person from the city of Corinth; also the name for some parts of the Bible (Corinthian, Corinthians)

corner = the angle where two lines, walls, or other surfaces meet; can mean to make a sharp turn while moving, or mean to stop someone and prevent them from moving; can mean a faraway place or region  (corner, corners, cornered, cornering)

corporal = a military officer ranked below sergeant and above a private; can mean ‘personal’ or having to do with the body; can mean punishment inflicted on the body

corps = a group of people with the same leader and purpose; often means a military branch, sometimes a unit that does special kinds of work 

corpse = a dead body, especially of a human (corpse, corpses; corpse-like)

corpse-hued = the color of a dead body

correspond = to match or agree in some way or form; to write a message; often means to exchange letters or to share information (correspond, corresponds, corresponded, corresponding; correspondence; correspondingly, correspondent, correspondents)

corridor = a place to walk or move; often means a hallway or a passageway; can mean a long strip of land or water allowing travel between two countries or areas corridor, corridors)

costly = expensive; sometimes means valuable, magnificent, sumptuous (costly, costlier, costliest; costliness)

cotton = a soft white plant fiber; can mean thread, cloth, or clothes or other things made from that fiber (cotton; cottony; cottonseed, cotton-seed)

cottage = a small house; often means a simple little house, sometimes in a country or rural setting (cottage, cottages)

cottonwood = a kind of poplar tree with seeds covered with fibers like hairs; can mean the wood of that tree (cottonwood, cottonwood-tree, cottonwood-trees)

couch = a divan; a piece of indoor furniture for one or more people to sit or lie down on; can mean any resting place; can mean to get ready to ambush someone, or to ready a weapon to attack (couch, couches, couched, couching)

council = a group of people gathered to discuss and make decisions for an organization (council, councils, councilman, councilwoman, councilor, councilors)

countenance = a person’s face or facial expression; the way something looks; can mean to agree with, accept, or support something (countenance, countenances)

counter = to oppose, to reject or refute; can mean contrary or opposite; can mean a person or device to keep track of numbers or scores; can mean a hard surface where one can put things (counter, counters, countered, countering)

countershot = a return shot made in answer to another shot; firing back during a battle  

country = a large portion of land outside of a city or town; a rural area; can mean a huge area or region where people live under one government (country, countries; countryside, country-side)

countrymen = people who were born in or live in the same country 

county-fairs = a kind of carnival, often with rides, food, exhibitions, and competitions, that is held once a year; a kind of big outdoor party for people from a certain county or region  (county-fair, county-fairs)

coup = a hit or blow; can mean a sudden, successful action; sometimes means an action to overthrow a government (coup, coups)

couple = a pair of things; two people who are a pair; can mean to link, join, or connect two things together; can sometimes mean to marry (couple, couples, coupled, coupling)

courier = someone who delivers letters, packages, or messages (courier, couriers)

courtier = someone who is part of a noble court; someone who uses flattery or friendly behavior as a way to get something (courtier, courtiers)

courtesy = good manners, politeness; can mean to do a favor (courtesies, courteous)

cousin = the son or daughter of your aunt or uncle; in olden times meant any kind of family member or relative (cousin, cousins)

covert = secret, hidden, concealed, or disguised (covert, covertly)

cower = to hide or cover oneself in fear; to behave in a cowardly way (cower, cowers, cowered, cowering)

cowl = a hood or a hooded robe with a loose neckline; can mean to put one on or to cover with a hood (cowl, cowls, cowled, cowling; cowled)

cozy = warm and comfortable; also means cloth put over a teapot to keep it warm (cozy, cozier, cozier, coziest; cozily)

crab = a beach animal with a wide flat body and a hard shell; or a machine for lifting heavy weights; or a kind of small, sour apple; can mean to have a bad temper, complain, or find fault (crab, crabs; crabby)

cracker = a thin, hard kind of biscuit that sometimes easily breaks into small pieces; can mean something that makes a sharp sound when it breaks or explodes; sometimes a slang term for a poor farmer (cracker, crackers; cracker-crumbs) 

crackle = a series of small snapping sounds; can mean fine lines on some pottery or glassware (crackle, crackles, crackling, crackled)

cradle = to hold or rock something gently; a baby’s rocking bed; can mean having to do with childhood or the beginning of something; can mean a framework for support (cradle, cradles, cradled, cradling)

cramp = a sharp tight muscle pain; can mean to hinder, limit, or prevent something (cramp, cramps, cramped, cramping)

crane = a tall wading bird with long legs and a long neck; can mean to stretch up and out; can mean a large machine for construction that carries and lifts items (crane, cranes, craned, craning)

crash = to fall, collide, or smash into something; to break or be destroyed from smashing into something; can mean a loud noise; can mean to fall, collapse, or be ruined (crash, crashes, crashing, crashed)

cravat = a necktie, often fancy; sometimes a neckcloth or scarf (cravat, cravats)

crave = to want very much; to desire intensely; to feel or have a great need; to ask or beg for something  (crave, craves, craved, craving; cravings)

craven = very cowardly; shamelessly afraid (craven; cravenly; cravenness)

crazy = to have a mental illness, be insane, deranged; can mean unreasonable, wild, or silly; can sometimes mean an extreme of something (crazy, crazier, craziest; crazily, craziness)

creak = a squeaking or grinding noise; to move and make such a noise (creak, creaks, creaked, creaking; creakings)

cream = the yellow, oily, fatty part of milk; the thick part of raw milk that rises to the top; can mean a thick lotion used on the skin; can mean to beat something until it has a smooth, thick consistency; can mean a yellowish white color (cream, creams; creamy)

crease = a line, mark, fold, or wrinkle made by bending cloth or paper; sometimes a dent made by heat or pressure; can mean a fired bullet that grazes or barely touches something  (crease, creases, creased, creasing)

creation = something that was made; something brought into existence; sometimes means everything that exists (creation, creations)

creature = a living person or animal (creature, creatures)

creditable = can be trusted; can mean praiseworthy or deserving recognition or belief (creditable, creditability)

creed = a set of beliefs, principles, or opinions; especially a set of religious beliefs (creed, creeds) 

creep = to move very quietly low to the ground, sometimes crawling or dragging the feet; to move hoping not to be seen; often means flowering plants with very long stems (creep, creeps, crept, creeping; creeper, creepers)

Creole = a person, language, food, or anything else caused by a mixture of two cultures; in Louisiana a descendant from the original French settlers (creole, creoles) 

crepe = a thin pancake; can also man thin cloth or paper; sometimes means the black clothing people worn in mourning when a loved one dies (crepe, crepes)

crescendo = sound, especially music, that gradually rises to a peak of loudness or intensity (crescendo, crescendos)

cress = green plants related to mustard, such as water cress, used in salads 

crest = a tuft of feathers, bone, or fur on an animal’s head; also a decoration displayed above the shield on a coat of arms, or any decoration that identifies something; can mean the highest point or to rise to a high point (crest, crests, crested, cresting)

criminal = someone who commits a crime; can mean illegal behavior (criminal, criminals)

crimp = to press something like cloth, paper, or dough into a pattern of small folds; to pleat; sometimes to make hair wavy, curly, or frizzy; can mean to limit or hinder (crimp, crimps, crimping, crimped; crimper; crimpy; crimpiness)

crimson = a deep red color (crimson, crimsoned)

cringe = to pull back in fear, or sometimes in disgust; to show great fear, to cower, to behave like a low creature without self-respect (cringe, cringes, cringed, cringing)

crinkle = to wrinkle, make wavy, or make ripples; can mean to make a rustling sound (crinkle, crinkles, crinkled, crinkling; crinkly, crinklier, crinkliest)

crisis = an unstable and uncertain situation; a great problem that needs a quick solution; an important turning point (crisis, crises)

crisp = firm but easy to break; can mean cool weather; sometimes means short and to the point (crisp; crispy; crisply)

crone = a hag, a withered old woman (crone, crones)

croquet = a game played on grass with mallets; players knock balls through a series of small arches called wickets (croquet, croqueted, croqueting)

cross = to move from one part to another; a mark like an X often to delete something; can mean to be angry or bad tempered; a T shape symbolic of Christianity; can mean to meet in passing; can mean to be opposed (cross, crosses, crossed, crossing)

crude = poorly done; can mean natural or raw, not refined or not cultured; sometimes means not having a skill; can mean to be rude (crude, cruder, crudest) 

cruel = extremely mean or evil; to purposely cause suffering; to be hardhearted, inhumane, or merciless (cruel, crueler, cruelest; cruelly; cruelness; cruelty, cruelties)

cruet = a small glass bottle with a stopper placed on a table to hold condiments such as vinegar or oil (cruet, cruets)

crust = a harder outside surface layer on something like bread, pie, snow, or mud; ‘crusty’ can also mean someone bad tempered or hard to get along with  (crust, crusts, crusted, crusting; crusty, crustier, crustiest)

crystal = a clear, transparent piece of very high quality glass or quartz stone; can mean tableware or other articles made from such material; can mean cut in a symmetrical arrangement (crystal, crystals; crystalline)

current = happening now; can mean water or air moving in one direction; can mean something common or commonly believed (current, currents; currently)

curtsey = a sign of respect when a person bends at the knee and dips the body slightly; in modern times practiced mostly by girls and women (curtsey curtsies, curtsied, curtseying)

doglike = resembling a dog in some way; having qualities that resemble those of a dog (doglike, dog-like) 
dogskin = leather made to look like dog’s skin, often used to make gloves
dogged = being persistent; not giving up (dogged; doggedly) 
doggerel = bad poetry; something that is poorly written 
doleful = acting unhappy; showing sadness (doleful; dolefully) 
domestic = having to do with how a family interacts or a home is managed; can sometimes means what happens inside a country, not affecting other countries; a ‘domestic’ workis in another person’s home (domestic; domestics) 
dominate = to strongly influence or control someone or something; can also mean the most important or most powerful thing (dominate, dominates, dominated, dominating; dominance, dominant) 
don = to put on or wear something (don, dons, donned, donning) 
door = a way to go in or out of a room, building, or vehicle; a place that is an entrance or exit (door, doors; doorway)
dooryard = a yard or garden near a house door  
dormer = a window that is sticks out, that is raised up on a sloping roof (dormer, dormers)
dormouse = a rodent that looks like a bushy-tailed mouse or a small squirrel; they sometimes hibernate (sleep for long periods), and have a reputation for being timid and easily frightened (dormouse, dormice) 
doth = does 
dot = a small round mark or spot; can mean to mark with a small spot or spots (dot, dots, dotted, dotting) 
double = two of something; sometimes means making twice as many, or happening twice as often (double, doubles, doubled, doubling) 
dove-cote = a kind of bird house with places for many different birds, especially for pigeons  (dove-cote, dove-cotes, dovecote, dovecotes)
downstairs = down a flight of stairs; can also mean the ground floor of a house or building (downstair, downstairs)

downward = going lower, toward a lower place, point, or level (downward, downwards) 
doze = to sleep or nap a little (doze, doze, dozes, dozing) 
draft = an early version of a piece of writing or drawing; can mean a light breeze; can mean to pull a load of something in a wagon or cart; sometimes means to select a person for a certain purpose (draft, drafts, drafted, drafting; drafty) 
drag = to pull something somewhere forcefully or roughly; to pull behind along the ground; can mean to lag behind or come slowly (drag, drags, dragged, dragging; draggingly) 
dragon = a pretend monster, often like a giant scaly lizard with big teeth, sometimes said to breathe fire (dragon, dragons) 
drain = to cause the water or liquid in something to run out; can mean the place it runs out; can also mean to make someone or something lose strength or energy (drain, drains, drained, draining) 
drama = a tv or movie story; can also mean an emotional series of events; sometimes means someone showing exaggerated emotions (drama, dramas; dramatic; dramatically) 
drape = the way a fabric or cloth hangs; can also mean to clothing loosely worn, or cloth or fabric covering or wrapped around something (drape, drapes, draped, draping) 
drapery = cloth, clothing, or curtains that hang loose (drapery, draperies) 
draught = British spelling of draft, which can mean a drawing or early piece of writing, or a light breeze, or to pull something in a wagon or cart, or be chosen for a job; ‘draughts’ is another name for the game of checkers (draught, draughts) 
drawbridge = a bridge with moving parts, usually over a castle’s moat or a river used by ships with tall masts; one section of a drawbridge can be raised or lowered to allow people or ships to pass over or under it (drawbridge, drawbridges)
drawing-room = a room in a home where guests can be entertained; in formal homes after dinner guests would withdraw to a room set apart for relaxing and talking (drawing-room, drawing-rooms)
drawl = a slow way of speaking, often with longer vowel sounds or leaving out some consonants; sometimes seen as a lazy way of speaking (drawl, drawls, drawled, drawling) 
dread = great fear or worry; often means to expect something terrible to happen (dread, dreads, dreaded, dreading; dreadful; dreadfully) 
dream =  thoughts, images, or feelings that occur in a person’s mind during sleep; can also mean a special goal, or something that a person would like to do or be (dream, dreams, dreamed, dreamt, dreaming; dreamy; dream-life) 
dreary = means gloomy, dull, dismal, depressing, wearisome (dreary; drearily; dreariness) 
dresser = a piece of furniture with drawers, usually for clothes; can also mean a person who dresses in a certain way, or who takes care of clothes for others and helps them put on clothes (dresser, dressers; dresser-drawer; dresser-shelf) 
dressing-room = a small room where people can change or try on clothes 
driblet = a thin stream or small drop of liquid; can also mean a small amount (driblet, driblets) 
dry = not wet, free from moisture; can also mean unexciting or dull; sometimes means a type of joke or humor; sometimes means not allowing the sale of alcohol (dry, dries, dried, drying; drier, driest) 
drift = carried slowly by air or water; can mean moving randomly from place to place; can be the way someone’s ideas or words are going; can mean a large mass of material moved by the wind or water (drift, drifts, drifted, drifting; drifter, drifter) 
drill = a tool used for making holes or to twist in screws; can be a type of repeated training, especially military training; (drill, drills, drilled, drilling) 
drinking-trough = a container for animals to drink from, often a long rectangular tank
droll = interesting in an offbeat, funny way (droll; drolly) 
droop = to bend or hang downward; can also mean acting sleepy (droop, droops, drooped, drooping; droopy; droopy-like)

drowsy = sleepy and lazy (drowsy, drowsier, drowsiest; drowsily; drowsiness) 
drug = a medicine that can help a sick person become more healthy; can mean some chemical that affects a person’s mind or body in a good or bad way (drug, drugs, drugged, drugging) 
drum = a musical instrument hit with sticks or the hands; often a hollow cylinder-shaped container; in olden times a ‘drummer’ was a salesman trying to ‘drum up’ business (drum, drums, drummed, drumming; drummer, drummers) 
drunken = having had too much alcohol, losing control (drunken; drunkenly; drunks)
dual = having two of the same, sometimes parts or elements that fit or work together; different from a ‘duel’ in which two people fight—sometimes to the death--according to special rules (dual; duality; dually) 
dub = give a name to someone or something, sometimes an unofficial name or nickname; can also mean when a king or ruler raises a soldier to the rank of knight (dub, dubs, dubbed, dubbing) 
duchess = a high-ranking woman, the wife or widow of a duke (duchess, duchesses) 
duck = a waterbird with a bill for lips, short legs, and webbed feet; can also mean to lower the head quickly to avoid being seen or being hit; a duck-pond is a small body of water for ducks (duck, ducks, ducked, ducking) 
duckling = a young duck (duckling, ducklings)
dud = something that fails to work properly, a failure; ‘duds’ is a slang word for clothes (dud, duds)

duet = a performance by two people, especially musicians or dancers (duet, duets)
duffer = someone not good at something; can mean someone who is stupid or awkward (duffer, duffers) 
dull = boring, not interesting or exciting; can also mean not bright or shiny; sometimes means slow to understand; can mean to make something less intense or bright or interesting (dull, dulls, dulled, dulling; duller, dullest; dully; dullard; dullness; dulness) 
dumfounded = greatly amazed, made unable to speak (dumbfounded, dumbfounding) 
dunce = someone slow at learning, or unable or unwilling to learn; not a polite word; in olden times a poor student would sometimes have to sit in a corner wearing a dunce-cap  (dunce, dunces) 
dun-colored = having a slightly brownish dark gray color 
dungeon = a strong prison cell, sometimes underground in a castle (dungeon, dungeons) 
dupe = to trick someone; can mean a victim of a trick (dupe, dupes, duped, duping) 
duration = the amount of time that something lasts or continues; 
dusky = darkish in color; can mean without much light, hard to see; can sometimes mean gloomy (dusky; duskily; duskiness) 
dust-cap = a cloth cap women used to wear when cleaning to protect their hair from dust and dirt; the hair, table tops, or other things could be ‘covered’ or ‘stained’ under a layer of dust (dust-cap, dust-caps, dustcap, dustcaps; dust-covered, dust-stained)   
dust = a dry powder made of tiny particles, often of dirt; can mean to remove the dust by wiping or brushing it; or sometimes means to sprinkle something powdery like sugar or flower on something (dust, dusts, dusted, dusting; duster, dusters) 
dustpan = a flat tool with a back into which a person can sweep dust, dirt, or other small things when cleaning; a ‘dustpanful’ is the full amount that a dustpan will hold (dustpan, dustpans; dustpanful)
dwarf = a pretend small person, sometimes magical, supposed to be good at mining or working metal; can mean anything smaller than usual; can mean something made to seem small or not important (dwarf, dwarfs, dwarfed, dwarfing; dwarves) 
dwell = to live in a place, or at a place; can sometimes mean to think or write about something (dwell, dwells, dwelt, dwelling; dwellings; dweller, dwellers) 
dwindle = to slowly become smaller, or less, or weaker (dwindle, dwindles, dwindled, dwindling)
eager = wanting to do or have something very much (eager; eagerly; eagerness) 
eagle-eye = staring hard at someone or something; can mean quick to notice things, or able to notice tiny things (eagle-eye, eagle-eyes; eagle-eyed)
eagle-fellows = a group of eagles; can mean other eagles or other kinds of eagles  
eagle = a large bird that eats smaller birds, animals, and fish, known for having good eyesight and powerful wings; an ‘eaglet’ is a young eagle (eagle, eagles, eaglet) 
eagle-vulture = a large black-and-white African bird with powerful wings and eyes like eagles, which, like vultures, often looks for dead animals to eat (eagle-vulture, eagle-vultures)
earl = a very high ranking English or British nobleman, usually rich and powerful (earl, earls) 
early =  happening or done before the usual or expected time; can also mean happening before a time period, or at the beginning of a time period (early, earlier, earliest) 
earnest = serious and intense; determined to do something; sometimes means showing a deep and intense belief or opinion (earnest; earnestness; earnestly) 
ear-smack = to hit someone on the ear; can mean to use both hands to clap both of someone’s ears at the same time (ear-smack, ear-smacks, ear-smacked, ear-smacking)
 earthlike = means 
earthly = having to do with life on earth, on our planet, sometimes in comparison to ‘heavenly’; the word ‘earthlike’ means similar to the earth, or like the earth (earthly, earthlike)
earthquake = a sudden shaking of the ground caused by powerful movements deep below; these often cause great damage to buildings, bridges, roads, and sometimes kill many people (earthquake, earthquakes; earthshaking) 
ease = to make something less hard, troublesome, severe, or difficult; sometimes means to move gently or carefully; to ‘take your ease’ means to relax (ease, eases, eased, easing) 
easy = without very much effort, not hard to do; can also mean time free from worry or problems, when a person can relax (easy, easier, easiest; easily) 
east = the direction where the sun rises in the morning; on most maps the right hand side; sometimes ‘the East’ means countries like China, Japan, Korea, India, Pakistan, or Bangladesh, or the eastern part of the world or of some certain area; can also mean something that is toward, near, or facing east (east, eastern; easterly) 
Easter = a Christian holiday in the spring time that celebrates the resurrection of Jesus Christ; on the holiday children often look for Easter eggs left by Easter bunnies
eave = the edge or edges of a roof hanging over the walls of a building (eave, eaves)
